    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText8615402301402670431" style="display:none"><b>STOP. </b>You should not have touched this flyer with your bare hands. NO, don't put it down. It's too late. They're watching you. <b>My name is David Wong.</b> My best friend is John. Those names are fake. You might want to change yours. You may not want to know about the things you'll read on these pages, about <b>the sauce</b>, about <b>Korrok</b>, about the invasion, and the future. But it's too late. You touched the book. You're in the game. You're under <b>the eye</b>. The only defense is knowledge. You need to read this book, to the end. Even the part with the bratwurst. Why? You just have to trust me.<br /><br /><b>The important thing is this: </b>The drug is called <b>Soy Sauce</b> and it gives users a window into another dimension. John and I never had the chance to say no. You still do. I'm sorry to have involved you in this, I really am. But as you read about these terrible events and the very <b>dark epoch</b> the world is about to enter as a result, it is crucial you keep one thing in mind: <b>
  <i>None of this was my fault.</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8615402301402670431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/959884-i-do-not-wish-to-be-rude-but-ya-know-so">I do not wish to be rude, but ya know, so many books so little time. So my question (at 10 pages in): Does it ever get less twee?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_959884'><a id="like_count_community_question_959884" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/959884?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F1857440.John_Dies_at_the_End">like</a></span>

</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/25055483-jordan-wk"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1382719850i/25055483.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/25055483-jordan-wk">Jordan Wk</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I'm not trying to be rude to you either, but it seems like you managed to pick the single adjective that in absolutely no way describes this book. Hm.<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I'm not trying to be rude to you either, but it seems like you managed to pick the single adjective that in absolutely no way describes this book. Hm. It's a lot of things and the things it is, it is extremely. <br /><br />Meandering? Yes<br />Self-aware? Self-indulgent<br />Sophomoric? Definitely<br />Convoluted? Surely<br /><br />But in spite of all of that, I really enjoyed it and think you should give it a chance. You will also probably enjoy the sequel more if your complaint is about the narrative flow. The sequel is far more cohesive, sober and focuses on a single story in the universe rather than following two deadbeats for over a year.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_93').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

<div id="review_306294977" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/306294977" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306294977?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306294977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14689400864182766554">Put this book down and go read Wong's work at cracked.com, particularly his piece "6 Things Rich People Need to Stop Saying," a brilliant piece of humor, psychology and economics. <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.cracked.com/blog/6-things-rich-people-need-to-stop-saying/'>http://www.cracked.com/blog/6-things-...</a><br/><br/>Back to <i> John Dies. </i> Yes, like the book blurb says, in some ways it resembles <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.The_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy__Hitchhiker_s_Guide___1_' title='The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (Hitchhiker's Guide, #1) by Douglas Adams' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a>--it's that strange blend of humor that occurs partially because of stacking two incongruencies in a slice of bread and calling it a sandwich. The heroes are similar </span>
  <span id="freeText14689400864182766554" style="display:none">Put this book down and go read Wong's work at cracked.com, particularly his piece "6 Things Rich People Need to Stop Saying," a brilliant piece of humor, psychology and economics. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.cracked.com/blog/6-things-rich-people-need-to-stop-saying/">http://www.cracked.com/blog/6-things-...</a><br /><br />Back to <i> John Dies. </i> Yes, like the book blurb says, in some ways it resembles <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.The_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy__Hitchhiker_s_Guide___1_" title="The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (Hitchhiker's Guide, #1) by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a>--it's that strange blend of humor that occurs partially because of stacking two incongruencies in a slice of bread and calling it a sandwich. The heroes are similar and somehwhat unlikeable; the rather boring Arthur Dent and 20-something slacker, David, a video store clerk. Both plots involve the end of the world as we know it, and time travel or alternate realities may or may not be involved. However, there are critical, fun-diminishing differences. Adams envisioned an entire universe for his absurdity while Wong plays around in modern America, where we've navel-gazed at absurdity so long, the commentary is hardly unique. Adams managed to turn the entire SF genre sideways with is originality, <i>John Dies </i> mostly feels like an unfinished stew of popular culture references and genre mashup. <br /><br />Why Hitchhiker's works: Vogon poetry. To appreciate the humor, he built a race entirely absent in emotional expression and vulnerability and then provided an example of their self expression, and the appropriate screams of horror from the audience.<br /><br />Why John Dies doesn't: two pages of random girlish chatroom transcript, complete with chat shorthand and exclamation points. With characters we haven't met or know nothing about but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ appear to be taken over by aliens by the end of chat. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Why Hitchhiker's works: exactly one exploding body, in the form of a sperm whale landing on a planet. It might be connected to a vase of petunias and have existential meaning.<br /><br />Why John Dies doesn't: numerous exploding bodies. Wet meaty chunks in various sizes throughout the book that have no meaning, except to impress us that people can die in a gross fashion.<br /><br />Why Hitchhiker's works: a robot so depressed, talking to him compels other machines to suicide, including life-support systems.<br /><br />Why John doesn't: waiting for a dog to poop so that the humans can retrieve a bomb. Aiming said dog's hind end at bad guy when he has burrito gut.<br /><br />Why Hitchhiker's works: white mice running experiments on the human race and threatening to carve up Arthur's brain.<br /><br />Why John doesn't: scorpion-tailed wig-wearing monsters stinging people.<br /><br />Why Hitchhiker's works: one ominous old man who looks a lot like a Biblical God, who creates fjords and completely fails at intimidation.<br /><br />Why John doesn't: numerous old and wrinkly men covered from the chest up, so the narrator can muse on sagging nether regions and greying pubic hair.<br /><br />There are certainly laugh-worthy and smart pieces. Loved the beginning brain puzzler with the ax and zombie. The meat puppet provided a groan-worthy pun. John channeling through a dog was amusing, as were the calming kittens. The occasional nicely-worded laugh. Comparing a downward, depressed slide in life to one's action playing sport video games.<br /><br />"I reached back and, for the first time in my life, smacked a dog across the nose with an envelope full of cash."<br /><br />"Things started to spin out of control. Soon we were playing (hockey) without the goalies... finally, when we started both playing on the same side (Red Wings) against an inept team controlled by the computer... I knew I had hit rock bottom."<br /><br />The language can be fun. But then there are the almost-but-not-quite analogies, such as the supposition if aliens had helped the Egyptians build a casino pyramid, it would look like the Luxor. Um, I believe that's the idea, more or less; a casino pyramid. I'm not sure myself how to take that to the next level of potential wierdness, but that's not it. <br /><br />And, of course, there's the toilet humor and penis imagery, a la movies like The Hangover. Clearly, I'm old, because it was funny for about a sentence, but unfortunately continued much longer. How many times can you freak out about grabbing penis doorknobs before you sound homophobic? Then there are the weird self-conscious references like, "now you've freaked out. Time to go start a website." Haha--just like the author. More distressing was the nagging deja vu feeling of "I think I recognize that scene from..." <br /><br />The characters were only mildly sympathetic, and John served as that zany foil that continued to lead our narrator astray. I felt like a lot of the situations were set up to get a laugh, which meant plot and narrative suffered. The tone struggled as well; I couldn't tell if I was supposed to be frightened, or tense as David found himself facing monsters or almost strangled, or if I should be waiting for the laugh. Since Wong went for the laugh almost every time, and his sense of humor doesn't entirely correspond with my own, it proved an ultimately unsatisfying read.<br /><br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2012/12/22/john-dies-at-the-end-by-david-wong/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2012/1...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14689400864182766554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_62198703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62198703" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62198703?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=bizarro">bizarro</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=humor-and-satire">humor-and-satire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62198703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10689538638328628393"><b>VERY HIP...</b><br/><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&current=John_Dies_At_The_End_review_article_story_main-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325378i/691051.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>VERY BIZARRO...</b><br/><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&current=john-dies2-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325378i/691052.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>VERY CREEPY...</b><br/><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&current=hands-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325378i/691053.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>AND VERY, VERY (EVEN BRILLIANTLY) FUNNY...IN A CRUDE, JUVENILE WAY...</b><br/><br/>I read a lot... I read everyday and go through a number of books every week. Reading as much as I do, I get a real jolly on when I come across a book like this because it is so different from the usual fare. I'm not sure I can adequately describe the book, but the phrase that seems most apt is <b>"brilliantly stupid"</b>…with "surreal,” "incredibly funny" and "dude that’s gross" clos</span>
  <span id="freeText10689538638328628393" style="display:none"><b>VERY HIP...</b><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&amp;current=John_Dies_At_The_End_review_article_story_main-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325378i/691051.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>VERY BIZARRO...</b><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&amp;current=john-dies2-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325378i/691052.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>VERY CREEPY...</b><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&amp;current=hands-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380325378i/691053.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>AND VERY, VERY (EVEN BRILLIANTLY) FUNNY...IN A CRUDE, JUVENILE WAY...</b><br><br>I read a lot... I read everyday and go through a number of books every week. Reading as much as I do, I get a real jolly on when I come across a book like this because it is so different from the usual fare. I'm not sure I can adequately describe the book, but the phrase that seems most apt is <b>"brilliantly stupid"</b>…with "surreal,” "incredibly funny" and "dude that’s gross" close behind. <blockquote>
<i>"Something coming back from the dead was almost always bad news. Movies taught me that. For every one Jesus you get a million zombies."</i> <br>…<br><i>"And watch out for Molly. See if she does anything unusual. There’s something I don’t trust about the way she exploded and then came back from the dead like that."</i>
</blockquote>...see what I mean.<br><br>As far as the plot, not much to say that isn't in the book description. David and John are a couple of smart, cynical, directionless guys. I think the book does such a great job speaking for itself, that here are a few excerpts from the book where David (our narrator) gives some insight into his worldview/mindset: <blockquote>
  <i> From day one it was like society was this violent, complicated dance and everybody had taken lessons but me. Knocked to the floor again, climbing to my feet each time, bloody and humiliated. Always met with disapproving faces, waiting for me to leave so I'd stop fucking up the party. <br>The wanted to push me outside, where the freaks huddled in the cold. Out there with the misfits, the broken, the glazed-eye types who can only watch as the normals enjoy their shiny new cars and careers and marriages and vacations with the kids. <br>The freaks spend their lives shambling around, wondering how they got left out, mumbling about conspiracy theories and bigfoot sightings. Their encounters with the world are marked by awkward conversations and stifled laughter, hidden smirks and rolled eyes. And worst of all, pity.</i>
</blockquote> AND later...<blockquote>
  <i>And no one cares. You kick and scream and cry out in the darkness and no answer comes. You rage against the unfathomable injustice and two blocks away some guy watches a baseball game and scratches his balls. <br>Scientists talk about dark matter, the invisible, mysterious substance that occupies the space between stars. Dark Matter makes up 99.99 percent of the universe and they don't know what it is. Well I know. It's apathy. That's the truth of it. Pile together everything we know and care about in the universe and it will still be nothing more than a tiny speck in the middle of a vast black ocean of Who Gives A Fuck. </i>
</blockquote> Well these two guys discover that a new drug called "soy sauce" has allowed/forced them to see into an alternative reality/parallel dimension where nasty, evil things with a good sense of humor are looking to take over (<u>See above</u> picture of a Roach-Man from the upcoming movie version). Well from the moment they experience the sauce, bizarroness and a mayhem-o-rama ensues. And I didn't stop laughing until the end. <br><br>The plot is utterly secondary to the reading experience and what shines in this book is the attitude of the two main characters, John and David, when they encounter the endless stream of nightmare situations in the book. They simply accept it, deal with it, shout out a lot of sarcasm and penis jokes and just go along for the ride. At least, for the most part…there are a few times when it gets to be a bit much for our heroes. Case in point: <blockquote>
  <i>“No, no. Keep driving,” said a soft voice in my ear. “She will not bite if you keep driving.” Fuck that. Fuck that idea like the captain of the Thai Fuck Team fucking at the fucking Tour de Fuck. </i>
</blockquote> However, other than a few understandable meltdowns (like when confronted by cockroach-man assassins), they simply attend to the matters at hand…no matter how batshit crazy things get (<i>"There was a sound like a garbage bag of pudding dropped off a tall building onto a sidewalk. Robert had erupted, chunks slapping off the walls in every direction."</i>)…UH, I did say it was gross didn't I? <br><br>My advice for this book is to be like John and David and just run with it. Don't try too hard to keep up with the plot and just let the story take you from page to page. I laughed out loud throughout the book and had a blast-o-matic reading it. For those of you still haven't come to appreciate the wit and tone of the book from my previous excerpts, here is my final attempt to win you over (the emphasis is mine): <blockquote> "Somebody said my name, asked if I was okay. I didn't answer, the sound of the commotion dying around me as <b>the heavy monkey of sleep rested its warm, furry ass on my eyelids</b>." </blockquote> Come on, now that is just funny. <br><br>In summary, this book is wonderful and strange, has a lot of juvenile humor, a couple of great main characters, and an original story in both plot and tone that I thought was brilliant…again is a stupid sorta way. Highly Recommended!! 4.5 to 5.0 stars.<br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10689538638328628393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Addie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Addie" href="/user/show/1689574-addie">Addie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312659141" href="/book/show/8017585-john-dies-at-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1689574-addie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269570797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8142192539253396026">This book is not for everyone but it is certainly for me.<br/><br/>We all know that I have the sense of humor of a twelve year-old boy. I can't help it. Just yesterday my manager was talking to my coworkers and I about her new job at Whole Foods, explaining what she would be doing (which is working behind the specialty cheese counter) and she spoke this little gem that slipped passed everyone's attention but mine: "...basically I'll be cutting the cheese all day." I slapped my hand to my mouth and trying </span>
  <span id="freeText8142192539253396026" style="display:none">This book is not for everyone but it is certainly for me.<br /><br />We all know that I have the sense of humor of a twelve year-old boy. I can't help it. Just yesterday my manager was talking to my coworkers and I about her new job at Whole Foods, explaining what she would be doing (which is working behind the specialty cheese counter) and she spoke this little gem that slipped passed everyone's attention but mine: "...basically I'll be cutting the cheese all day." I slapped my hand to my mouth and trying to hide my giggles only made them come even more fitfully.<br /><br />I'm laughing right now just thinking about it!<br /><br />That's not really an important point, but I am a big fan of dick and fart jokes in all facets of life, and this books' cup runneth over with them, much to my enjoyment. My potential favorite: "Every man is blessed with his gifts from the Lord. One of mine happens to be a penis large enough that, if it had a penis of its own, my penis's penis would be larger than your penis." 2nd place: "I want to pause for a moment to talk about my penis" and the ensuing section comparing sex to Disney World. Verrry close 3rd place: John's whole "I'd show [my penis] right now, to everybody here. If we had time..." speech.<br /><br />It's not a perfect book, but I don't care. Fuck the kind of pretension that doesn't allow a person to just sit back and enjoy this story. The whole thing was a riot. I totally loved it, if for no other reason than it came to me when I needed it most, a la the sword of Gryffindor. I have been reading Tolkien since the end of last summer, and it has been wonderful, really, but it's so dense and demanding that lately I have been really feeling the need to take a break and read something a little less serious. I found this at the bookstore, popped it open to see what I was in for, then wouldn't put it down. If I believed in the power of prayer, I would say that finding this book when I did was the answer to one. Thanks, universe! I owe you one!<br /><br /><br /><u>Addendum:</u> I'm sorry to all of the ladies out there in the world, but this book helped me to realize that, as much as I long to be taken seriously as a woman of thought and value, I am never going to be able to stop thinking that farts are funny. I'm just not. Books like this will always have a special place in my heart, even if they don't make me any smarter. I just have to accept that part of myself.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8142192539253396026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Traci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Traci" href="/user/show/5024825-traci">Traci</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462970076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15206204225008406483">Have you ever played that game when one person starts a story and then another person takes it over, and then another, and then...until the story gets to where you can't even remember how it started? <br/><br/>John Dies at the End is a little bit like that game.<br/><br/>Now picture Howard Philip Lovecraft and Robert E. Howard playing this game around a campfire after a crazy party. <br/><br/>Now picture Howard Philip Lovecraft and Robert E. Howard smoking pot and drinking cheap booze as they play the game. <br/><br/>And then they are</span>
  <span id="freeText15206204225008406483" style="display:none">Have you ever played that game when one person starts a story and then another person takes it over, and then another, and then...until the story gets to where you can't even remember how it started? <br /><br />John Dies at the End is a little bit like that game.<br /><br />Now picture Howard Philip Lovecraft and Robert E. Howard playing this game around a campfire after a crazy party. <br /><br />Now picture Howard Philip Lovecraft and Robert E. Howard smoking pot and drinking cheap booze as they play the game. <br /><br />And then they are joined by their good friends Joss Whedon and Todd Phillips.<br /><br />John Dies at the End is what they might come up with. <br /><br />I wanted to like this book. Really, really, really, wanted to like it. And maybe that was part of the problem. I went in with too high of expectations. Shrug. But honestly it just wasn't for me. <br /><br />Recommended to readers who still laugh at the jokes they thought were funny when they were twelve. Fans of urban fantasy/horror that does not involve sparkly vampires. And for anyone who thought Cabin In the Woods was one of the best movies of the year.<br /><br />As for the title...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The cake is a lie <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_1288068754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288068754" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1288068754?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8242493-john-dies-at-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2020">year-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288068754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4588505420022427995"><b>This book is about <u>shit.</u> And <u>insects.</u> And <u>humanity.</u></b><br/><br/>A peculiar combination, you may think? I agree. But this is a great story that may not have worked in the hands of any other author.<br/><br/>My most amazing cousin <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52417483-danielle-cart' rel='nofollow noopener'>Danielle</a> has been asking me to read this book for about a year now, and I'm really glad I <u>finally</u> picked it up. <br/><br/><b>It's packed with meat monsters, immortal dogs, & exploding eyeballs with a fake Jamaican cherry on top!</b><br/><br/>While all these aspects make for some <b>top-level ridiculousness,</b> I think it's im</span>
  <span id="freeText4588505420022427995" style="display:none"><b>This book is about <u>shit.</u> And <u>insects.</u> And <u>humanity.</u></b><br /><br />A peculiar combination, you may think? I agree. But this is a great story that may not have worked in the hands of any other author.<br /><br />My most amazing cousin <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52417483-danielle-cart" rel="nofollow noopener">Danielle</a> has been asking me to read this book for about a year now, and I'm really glad I <u>finally</u> picked it up. <br /><br /><b>It's packed with meat monsters, immortal dogs, &amp; exploding eyeballs with a fake Jamaican cherry on top!</b><br /><br />While all these aspects make for some <b>top-level ridiculousness,</b> I think it's important not to let them totally distract from the <b>messages</b> that are present.<br /><br />The writing is what really brought the story to life. It's told from the perspective of David, who is incredibly witty &amp; has a lot of insightful things to say about why humans behave the way they do. Sure, he is disparaging &amp; crude in his commentary, but there's a ribbon of raw truth beneath it all that makes David an intensely relatable character.<br /><br />It's almost uncomfortable how Wong forces his audience to face the juxtaposition of deeply relevant ideas next to a black, self-depreciating humor &amp; a consistent stream of stomach-churning violence. <b>But it's cleverly constructed &amp; mostly positive experience.</b> <br /><br />The plot of this one is <b>strange.</b> <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Like, super strange.</i>
</b><br /><br />There were a couple times where it lost my <i>complete</i> attention. I would catch myself sort of glossing over some of the filler details of the scenario, but on the whole I still found it enjoyable. <br /><br />Also I must say I'm relieved to read an Epilogue that I won't have to spend the rest of my life pretending doesn't exist. <i>Lookin' at you Rowling.</i><br /><br />One other thing I didn't love about this book was it's use of offensive language. I can tell that it was used to characterize &amp; set a tone of cynicism, but it was a little too liberally applied for my tastes. <br /><br />I wanted to add this as more of a caution for others because truthfully there's a <b>ton of offensive stuff in this book,</b> but the language in particular made me grit my teeth a couple of times. I was still able to enjoy the story, but it's worth mentioning. <br /><br />This is going to be a novel I will recommend with a discerning eye. No doubt this story will be too contemptuous for some to swallow (that one's for you John), but if a bizarre horror/comedy/mystery with a dash of philosophical genius &amp; sprinkling of extra-fucking-weird sounds up your alley then <b>this is a book for you!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4588505420022427995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1288068754">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623508629" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/623508629?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer623508629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6252885368290298611">Juvenile humor was only a feature of this novel, not a bug. There were plenty of bugs, tho. That being said, it was a light-hearted frolic in the woods of shit-narnia, and I felt like getting a tattoo of the Pi symbol on my toe. Strangely enough, I agreed with the idea of the last dead guy that first-person shooter games are training us for something... but I just can't figure out what it was... better game-playing? That's probably it. <br/><br/>This is a Fun Book, ya'll, even if I was expecting something</span>
  <span id="freeText6252885368290298611" style="display:none">Juvenile humor was only a feature of this novel, not a bug. There were plenty of bugs, tho. That being said, it was a light-hearted frolic in the woods of shit-narnia, and I felt like getting a tattoo of the Pi symbol on my toe. Strangely enough, I agreed with the idea of the last dead guy that first-person shooter games are training us for something... but I just can't figure out what it was... better game-playing? That's probably it. <br /><br />This is a Fun Book, ya'll, even if I was expecting something SCARY. Not scary, but quite imaginative with more plot holes than a termite could cope with. That's OK, you know, as long as you have a good time. :)<br /><br />But like I said, that's a feature, not a bug. But oh my god... The Bugs! The Bugs!</span>

<div id="review_1554546262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1554546262" />
    <a title="Poonam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17656456-poonam"><img alt="Poonam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520691179p2/17656456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1554546262?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Poonam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Poonam" href="/user/show/17656456-poonam">Poonam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=mystery-thriller-suspense">mystery-thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=paranormal-or-fantasy">paranormal-or-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1554546262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6063074088547504261"><b>
  <i>"This stopped me. The cops called us? What, they got a ghost they want us to check out? Like we're fucking Scooby-Doo?"</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Premise:</b> David Wong and his friend John are kind of ghost-busters, they see things that others can't. This is because of a drug that they have consumed which is named soya-sauce for the lack of a better name and it does look a bit like that (apparently). <br/><br/><b>I liked it at the start. I really did.</b> The jokes, the way the horror and humor were combined made me keep on turning the p</span>
  <span id="freeText6063074088547504261" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"This stopped me. The cops called us? What, they got a ghost they want us to check out? Like we're fucking Scooby-Doo?"</i>
</b><br><br><b>Premise:</b> David Wong and his friend John are kind of ghost-busters, they see things that others can't. This is because of a drug that they have consumed which is named soya-sauce for the lack of a better name and it does look a bit like that (apparently). <br><br><b>I liked it at the start. I really did.</b> The jokes, the way the horror and humor were combined made me keep on turning the pages. There were lots of action scenes and the story reached it's climax. I thought we are done and it would have been a good ending but then the author decided<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493030311ra/22576742.gif" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The <b>Part 2</b> of the book commenced. The story started feeling disjointed and I was losing track as to how all this is connected to the first part. It started getting frustrating, the jokes got old, the action scene started getting dis-interesting. And finally when I thought this book is going to get over...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493031040ra/22576810.gif" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We started with the <b>Part 3!!</b>. This was the part where I actually thought of DNFing the book but some perverse sense of self-torture made me continue reading this. I had completed around 60% of the book and did not want to abandon this. I also really wanted to know how the author is going to wrap up this trainwreck of a story. The Epilogue itself was soo big that I just wanted it to be over. Skimming through the book made even less sense of what I was reading as the story just jumped around and I had to read everything like a good little girl.<br><br><b>Did the ending make sense?</b>- Yes, yes it did.<br><br>Will I be picking up the next book of this series?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493031610ra/22576882.gif" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6063074088547504261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1826745204" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826745204" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1826745204?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826745204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16698172316634174220"><i>“The man-shaped arrangement of meat rose up, as if functioning as one body. It pushed itself up on two arms made of game hens and country bacon, planting two hands with sausage-link fingers on the floor. The phrase “sodomized by a bratwurst poltergeist” suddenly flew through my mind. Finally it stood fully upright, looking like the mascot for a butcher shop whose profits went entirely to support the owner’s acid habit.”</i><br/><br/>The above quote from the prologue sets the tone very nicely for <i>John Dies at </i></span>
  <span id="freeText16698172316634174220" style="display:none"><i>“The man-shaped arrangement of meat rose up, as if functioning as one body. It pushed itself up on two arms made of game hens and country bacon, planting two hands with sausage-link fingers on the floor. The phrase “sodomized by a bratwurst poltergeist” suddenly flew through my mind. Finally it stood fully upright, looking like the mascot for a butcher shop whose profits went entirely to support the owner’s acid habit.”</i><br><br>The above quote from the prologue sets the tone very nicely for <i>John Dies at the End</i>. It really is a wild ride of a book. I became interested in this book a few years ago when I heard it was being <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1783732/" rel="nofollow noopener">adapted into a movie</a> back in 2012. The title alone is quite intriguing; here is a book that seems to spoil its own ending from the title, that is something new. Of course, the title does not really spoil the book but it is a damn good hook. I added it on my TBR and it languished there for several years. I think it was priced quite expensively at the time, something over USD 10 for a 376 pages book, so I put it on the backburner. A couple of weeks ago Amazon offered the e-book for a limited time at USD 2.76 so I was quite happy to snap it up.<br><br><i>John Dies at the End</i> is more about David Wong—the character, not the author*—than it is about John. Dave and John are besties in the <s>grand</s> <i>Excellent!</i> tradition of Bill and Ted.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481383471i/21417491._SX540_.png" width="400" height="218" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>David Wong, in spite of the name, is not Chinese, he prefers to use a pseudonym for the sake of anonymity. At the beginning of the book, it seems that John and Dave are some kind of Ghostbusters who are called to investigate or exorcise spirits, demons or any kind of supernatural entities. As a pair of paranormal investigators, they are more similar to Sam and Dean Winchester from the CW series “Supernatural” than the Ghostbusters team or The X-Files’ Mulder and Scully. After the encounter with the Meat Monster in the prologue, the narrative rewinds to the beginning of their paranormal investigation career. John and Dave are exposed to a weird substance nicknamed “Soy Sauce” that enables them to see supernatural or pandimensional beings from other dimensions. Immediately they become embroiled in a plot by shadowy beings to corrupt and take over our reality. <i>John Dies at the End</i> is basically the story of the duo’s struggle to save the world.<br><br>The main body of the narrative is nested inside a frame story where Dave is being interviewed by a reporter who specializes in paranormal stories. From beginning to end it is a very fast-paced narrative, and never really slow down to take a breather. I usually enjoy fast paced page turners but I feel it is overdone here. Incident piles upon incident in rapid succession, not much time is spent on expositions or character development. I felt like I was hanging on to the narrative by the skin of my teeth. This has the ironic effect of the book becoming a little monotonous toward the end. On the plus side there are quite a lot of bizarre sights to see; wig monsters, gigantic blobby monsters, flying parasites, ghosts, clones, exploding dogs and policemen, copious amount of blood and poo etc. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481383471i/21417492._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="257" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Wig Monsters <a href="http://flammableperson.deviantart.com/art/The-WigMonsters-Emerge-John-Dies-at-the-End-475193245" rel="nofollow noopener">by FlammablePerson</a><br><br>There is also an unpleasant parallel dimension our heroes amusingly name “Shit Narnia”. There is plenty to keep me interested, but not a lot to care about. I think it comes down to characterization. John and Dave are likable enough duo with their bantering, flippant attitude, defiance of authority and penis jokes. However, I feel that there is insufficient depth to them to carry almost 400 pages of narrative. Thankfully there is a little bit of romance between Dave and a girl called Amy which provides a nice bit of light and shade to the inexorable narrative. It also gives Dave an opportunity to become a hero instead of a smartass.<br><br>The prose style seems to be aimed at teenaged boys, however, the often NSFW adolescent humour did make me chuckle quite a few times. The author writes a bit like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6540057.Andy_Weir" title="Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener"> Andy Weir</a> on speed, though, for me, the humour here works better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Martian</a>. My only complaint is the relentless pacing which sometimes makes the narrative feel overly chaotic and even a bit of a mess. It becomes oddly exhausting toward the end of the book. Even the epilogue seems excessively long and the pacing is still not winding down. While reading the last twenty or so pages I felt the book outstayed it's welcome a little; I suspect 300 pages would have been just right. <br><br>Having said all that I don’t want to give the impression that <i>John Dies at the End</i> is bad or dull. It is a fun book, possibly ideal for readers with short attention span, or those looking for nonstop thrills. I don’t think I am on board for the sequel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12924261.This_Book_Is_Full_of_Spiders_Seriously__Dude__Don_t_Touch_It__John_Dies_at_the_End___2_" title="This Book Is Full of Spiders Seriously, Dude, Don't Touch It (John Dies at the End, #2) by David Wong" rel="nofollow noopener"> This Book Is Full of Spiders: Seriously, Dude, Don't Touch It</a>, but it has a higher GR rating than this book so I may change my mind later if I fancy reading something wild. Certainly, I have no regret reading this book. If you are looking for a funny, wild, and anarchic sci-fi horror adventure this could do very well. If you are cautious perhaps you can try a sample chapter from Amazon, the book does start with a bang, and the prologue is quite representative of the entire book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481383471i/21417493._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="41" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>* The author's use of the David Wong pen name lends his first person narration an air of verisimilitude, and a "meta" feel. His real name, Jason Pargin, is no secret, it is mentioned in the introduction to the book, written by eccentric filmmaker, Don Coscarelli, who directed the film adaptation and also a few weird movies like Phantasm and Bubba Ho-Tep.<br>____________________<br><br><b>Quotes</b><br><i>If I had known what was about to happen at work I wouldn’t have gone, of course. I would also have taken off my pants.<br><br>Something coming back from the dead was almost always bad news. Movies taught me that. For every one Jesus you get a million zombies.<br><br>“You have tormented me six times. Now prepare to meat your doom!” I have no way of knowing that it actually said “meat” instead of “meet” but I’ll give it the benefit of the doubt. I ran.<br><br>“Good. Anyway, Amy is missing and the scene is weird as shit. The situation has a real Lovecraft feel to it. Though, you know, if you come over it’ll be more of an Anne Rice situation. If you know what I mean. Because you’re gay.”<br><br>“Dave? It’s me. Amy’s missing and we got what looks like a bag full of fat here. It’s weird. And I mean ‘bad’ weird, not ‘clown’ weird.<br><br>There was a time when I would have found the idea of certain death a little comforting, like being on the last day of a job I hated.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481383471i/21417494._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="267" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>The Meat Monster from the movie adaptation</span>
  <a data-text-id="16698172316634174220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2505131464?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2505131464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13705984823495822591">A tangled quagmire of whatthehell.<br/><br/>Reminiscent of Hunter S. Thompson and maybe William Burroughs, this eschews stream of consciousness but revels in surrealism and absurdity. Telling a Lovecraftian / Ghostbusters tale, at best it is fun and well crafted, at worst it devolves into a prolonged fart joke.<br/><br/>Interestingly, this began as a web serial back in 2001 with tens of thousands of fans enjoying the snark for free before it was finally all put together in a paperback in 2007. The online versions w</span>
  <span id="freeText13705984823495822591" style="display:none">A tangled quagmire of whatthehell.<br><br>Reminiscent of Hunter S. Thompson and maybe William Burroughs, this eschews stream of consciousness but revels in surrealism and absurdity. Telling a Lovecraftian / Ghostbusters tale, at best it is fun and well crafted, at worst it devolves into a prolonged fart joke.<br><br>Interestingly, this began as a web serial back in 2001 with tens of thousands of fans enjoying the snark for free before it was finally all put together in a paperback in 2007. The online versions were removed in 2008.<br><br>Like a ten-minute Saturday Night Live skit stretched out to make a two-hour movie, much of the laugh out loud hilarity of the first 50 pages are diluted by the end. To his credit, author David Wong produces many smiles and giggles along the way and also explores some serious themes of bullying and social justice. These islands of clarity and sober introspection keep this from flying off the pages into a sophomoric mess.<br><br>Still fun and overall an enjoyable read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554481855i/27320113.jpg" width="220" height="326" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13705984823495822591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_290168626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/290168626" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290168626?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=horror-esque">horror-esque</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290168626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3449948161148023175">2.5<br/><br/>So... Um... Well, that was, erm, something all right... <br/><br/>So I suppose I should start off by saying it's not quite what I was expecting but, of course, the logical follow-up to that would be "well, what were you expecting?", and I'd have to say "I'm not really sure. But that wasn't it."<br/><br/>But I think one thing I was expecting was a different kind of humor. Maybe something more along the lines of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33456.A_Dirty_Job__Grim_Reaper___1_' title='A Dirty Job (Grim Reaper, #1) by Christopher Moore' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Dirty Job</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16218.Christopher_Moore' title='Christopher Moore' rel='nofollow noopener'>Christopher Moore</a>, or even 'Army of Darkness' with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1362939.Bruce_Campbell' title='Bruce Campbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bruce Campbell</a>.<br/><br/>Not to say it didn't h</span>
  <span id="freeText3449948161148023175" style="display:none">2.5<br /><br />So... Um... Well, that was, erm, something all right... <br /><br />So I suppose I should start off by saying it's not quite what I was expecting but, of course, the logical follow-up to that would be "well, what were you expecting?", and I'd have to say "I'm not really sure. But that wasn't it."<br /><br />But I think one thing I was expecting was a different kind of humor. Maybe something more along the lines of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33456.A_Dirty_Job__Grim_Reaper___1_" title="A Dirty Job (Grim Reaper, #1) by Christopher Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">A Dirty Job</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16218.Christopher_Moore" title="Christopher Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">Christopher Moore</a>, or even 'Army of Darkness' with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1362939.Bruce_Campbell" title="Bruce Campbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Bruce Campbell</a>.<br /><br />Not to say it didn't have humor. It had a lot of wry dialogue and snarky asides and random absurdity - which I generally liked - and also a lot of frat-boy type dick humor - which, not so much.<br /><br />It also had a lot of gore, and action, and gore, and haphazard plotting, and gore, and weirdness, and did I mention gore?<br /><br />It's a book where, when I read it and was able to get into the actual plot-line of strange things from another dimension trying to break their way into ours, I could actually go along for the ride and be kind of scared and disturbed and sort of enjoy the general wtf-osity of the whole thing.<br /><br />But when I put the book down I didn't really feel much impetus to put it back up. I didn't really connect with the characters or <i>care</i> so much about what was going on, though, as I said, it was interesting and kind of cool when I was reading it.<br /><br />But it seemed to drag a lot in the middle, mostly because of this lack of care, and it felt just generally repetitive - David tries to ignore shit while John seeks it out, David gets caught up in the action, shit goes down, things blow up for no apparent reason except that it's cool that things should blow up in the most gruesome way possible, the day is saved, things settle down, rinse, wash, repeat.<br /><br />It got kind of blah after awhile, and even the weirdness and gore didn't have much of an effect aside from "oh look, there's more".<br /><br />But it shifted towards the end and started to shift focus onto the characters and people and things actually mattering, and I started to feel invested in the story. I was on tenterhooks, towards the end, waiting for the other proverbial shoe to drop, and then... <br /><br />Well, that would be spoilery.<br /><br />But I will say that it definitely got a bit more cohesive at the end but, overall, I think it could've been tighter and less rambly and while I did sort of generally like it, overall, I still feel no real compulsion to get back into it and I doubt I'd actively seek out the next book that is, apparently, in the making.<br /><br />I might see the movie, though. (2.75 stars)</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_443302679" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/443302679" />
    <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party"><img alt="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562621595p2/10923016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/443302679?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party">David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8242493-john-dies-at-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=make-me-laugh">make-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=whoa-thats-messed-up">whoa-thats-messed-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=read-by-kindlelight">read-by-kindlelight</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer443302679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15838703064025663453"><i>Don't let the spoilerish title fool you... </i><b>John Dies At The End</b><i> is full of surprises!</i> <br/> <br/>Life is full of millions of choices. And while some are instantly recognized as "life-choices" (like getting married or picking a career path), others are deceptively innocent. But even the smallest of choices can have huge consequences. That's the hard lesson David Wong learned when he decided to challenge a hack street-magician at a concert. Had Wong simply rolled his eyes and kept walking, his life may not </span>
  <span id="freeText15838703064025663453" style="display:none"><i>Don't let the spoilerish title fool you... </i><b>John Dies At The End</b><i> is full of surprises!</i> <br> <br>Life is full of millions of choices. And while some are instantly recognized as "life-choices" (like getting married or picking a career path), others are deceptively innocent. But even the smallest of choices can have huge consequences. That's the hard lesson David Wong learned when he decided to challenge a hack street-magician at a concert. Had Wong simply rolled his eyes and kept walking, his life may not have turned into the horror story it became. We all make millions of choices, and any one of them can ruin our lives forever...now THAT is true horror!<br> <br>I was very pleasantly surprised by <i>"John Dies At The End"</i> Having read many of his articles on <i>Cracked.com</i>, I knew David Wong possessed a great sense of humor, so I fully expected his book to be funny, but what I wasn't anticipating is how great he is at writing horror as well! Wong's imagination is almost limitless, as he manages to concoct some of the most bizarre creatures I've ever read about, and his ability to channel fear and dread is so strong, it's unfathomable to me that this is his first novel! In fact, I would have loved to have given this book five stars, but there was one problem that constantly detracted from my enjoyment...<i>it's gross...it's really, really gross!</i> As much as there is to admire about this book, the non-stop barrage of potty humor and crudeness makes it a difficult one to recommend to people...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395720ra/762216.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="anieww" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>This girl would not get past page 5 of "John Dies At The End"!</i><br> <br>After a prologue which expertly depicts the bizarre world David Wong lives in, the majority of the book is comprised of two flashback sequences that explain how Dave's life has gotten to this point. The two flashbacks are bridged together by a framing sequence involving a present-day conversation Dave is having with a reporter who is investigating Dave's claim to be some kind of "monster-hunter". The rather unconventional story structure is just part of the book's charm, as Wong's narrative keeps flipping from past to present, yet it rarely gets confusing and Wong often peppers it with some tantalizing foreshadowing. The first segment covers Dave's first foray into the paranormal, in which he's joined by his smart-ass friend John. After he taunts a wannabe magician as an obvious hoax, Dave is exposed to a substance that seems peculiarly like soy sauce, yet the phony magician claims it will actually expose Dave to the world of the supernatural...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395720i/762217._SX540_.jpg" width="325" height="250" alt="soysauce" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>One drop of this magical soy sauce will have a horrible effect on your body...actually, that's kinda how I feel about regular soy sauce, too!</i><br> <br>Soon after experiencing the soy sauce of doom, Dave's world falls apart. He begins to see grotesque creatures all around him. People in his life are brutally murdered and Wong finds himself the chief suspect (sometimes even in his own eyes). Soon Dave and John learn that something from another world wants to enter our own, something truly evil and deadly. Thus begins their often-hilarious quest to save our world from a malicious entity of Lovecraftian proportions. Between John's <i>"so-stupid-it's-funny"</i> humor, and Dave's rapier wit, I was howling with laughter throughout most of the first segment.<br> <br>After the events of the first segment, Dave &amp; John try to get back to what I'll generously refer to as their <i>"normal"</i> lives, which leads to the second segment, where they soon discover that evil from another world is still trying to invade ours...but this time they're targeting Dave and John directly. The second segment doesn't have as much humor as the first, but it more than makes up for this in dramatic storytelling. In the second story, the battle is much more personal and the stakes are much higher. It's here that Wong's talent as an author truly shines. While he already displayed much creativity and wit in the first half, Wong manages to invoke more emotions to tell a very powerful story in the second half. At times, reading this was like a greatest hits collection of the works of Christopher Moore and Stephen King, the way Wong could blend humor and horror together and give equal weight to both genres. All in all, this was an amazing book to read...<i>except...</i><br> <br>Look, let's get something out of the way, I'm hardly a prude. My tastes aren't exactly sophisticated, and I've been known to chuckle at a tasteless joke or two...<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395720i/762218._SY540_.jpg" width="275" height="375" alt="teenmovie" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>I think <b>Not Another Teen Movie</b> is one of the funniest comedies ever made...please tell no one of this!</i> <br> <br>That being said, I did find the gross-out factor of this book to be beyond excessive. There are so many poop jokes, even Beavis and Butt-Head would find this book to be a bit much. And while I applaud Wong's vast imagination in creating new horrors, at times it seems like he's just trying too hard to disgust his readers. In addition to potty humor, Wong displays an almost-obsessive fascination with insects (one segment even involves a man made entirely out of cockroaches), and just when you think Wong can't possibly manage to make bugs any more gross, he finds a way to top himself. It can be almost infuriating, as Wong clearly has a true talent for horror. In his best moments, Wong shows great promise and depth as a writer, which makes it all the more baffling why he felt the need to take such a juvenile approach at times...<br> <br>If you have a love for dark comedy (as well as a really strong stomach), <i>"John Dies At The End"</i> should be a wild ride for you. However, anyone who's even a bit squeamish (particularly when it comes to insects and...y'know, that bodily function no one ever talks about in polite company) may want to avoid this one. Still, considering his undeniable talent, if David Wong can reign in his love for toilet humor, I have no doubt one of his books will make it on my "Favorites" shelf some day! <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15838703064025663453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
